باسمه تعالی
تقريظ :
حضرت مولانا مفتی محمد یوسف صاحب تا دلی مد ظلہ العالی خادم حدیث دارالعلوم دیوبند
حامداً ومصليا اما بعد:
الاشباہ والنظائر ابن نجیم مصری کی بہت مشہور کتاب اور افتاء کے کورس میں داخل
نصاب ہے۔
مکرم و محترم جناب مفتی محمد معصوم صاحب قاسمی نے بہت سہل انداز میں اردو زبان میں شرح کی ہے، ان شاء اللہ کتاب طلبہ کے لئے مفید ثابت ہوگی حق تعالٰی جناب موصوف کی خدمت کو قبول فرمائے اور مزید خدمات کی توفیق عطا فرمائے ۔ ( آمین یا رب العالمین)
محمد یوسف تا ولی خادم حدیث دارالعلوم دیوبند

تقريظ
جناب مولانا محمد شکیب صاحب قاسمی ناظم حجت الاسلام اکیڈمی د استاذ دار العلوم وقف دیوبند
انسان کی وجہ تخلیق پر غور کیجئے ، انسان کو کیوں پیدا کیا گیا، کیا کسب معاش انسان کا مقصد تخلیق ہے یا تسخیر کائنات کے لئے وہ دنیا میں لایا گیا، اونچی اونچی فلک بوس عمارت اور نا قابل تسخیر قلعے تعمیر کرنا اس کی زندگی کا مقصد ہے یا وہ اس زمین دنیا کی لذتوں سے لطف اندوز ہونے کے لئے پیدا ہوا ہے۔ قرآن حکیم کا اعلان یہ ہے وَمَا خَلَقْتُ الْجِنَّ وَالإِنْسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونَ“ جب خدا وند قدوس کی عبادت ہی انسان کا مقصد تخلیق ٹھہرا تو پھر اس مقصد کو مکمل طور پر حاصل کر لینا ہی انسان کی نجات کا ضامن ہے۔ انسان عبادت کیسے کرے اور اپنی بندگی کا ثبوت بارگاہ خداوندی میں کیسے پیش کرے؟ ظاہر ہے اس کے لئے احکام شریعت کا بھر پور علم ضروری ہے تا کہ وہ اپنے مقصد میں کامیاب وکامران ہو سکے۔ اندازہ کیجئے جو اسلام کے احکام سے بے خبر ہو، جو فقہ اسلامی سے نا آشنا ہو، جس کا ذہن دینی شعور سے نابلد ہو وہ اپنے مقصد زندگی سے کتنا دور ہے؟ حدیث رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم "من يرد الله به خيراً يفقه في الدين" کے صرف اس پہلو کو پیش نظر مت رکھئے کہ اللہ رب العزت جس کے ساتھ بھلائی کا معاملہ کرنا چاہتے ہیں، اسے دین کی سمجھ عطا کر دیتے ہیں بلکہ اس پہلو پر بھی نظر رہنا ضروری ہے کہ جس نے دین کی سمجھ نہیں حاصل کی تو اللہ تعالی کا اس کے ساتھ کیسا معاملہ ہو گا ؟ غرض یہ کہ انسان اپنے مقصد تخلیق کی تکمیل اس وقت تک کامل طور نہیں کر سکتا جب تک وہ علم فقہ سے مناسبت نہ پیدا کر لے۔ علم فقہ کے تعلق سے قرآن و حدیث میں جو کچھ بھی ہے وہ اس علم کی اہمیت کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے کافی ہے، ہر دور میں اس کی اہمیت کو سمجھا گیا، اس کی ضرورت کو سمجھا گیا اور ہر زمانے میں لوگوں نے اسے سیکھا اور سکھایا ہے۔ اس فن کے ماہرین نے ابتدائی دور میں اس فن کی تدوین کے لئے اپنی زندگیاں وقف کیں، اپنا سرمایہ صرف کیا اور اس عظیم الشان علم کو آسان کر کے امت کو پیش کرتے رہے ۔
In the name of Allah the Exalted. Endorsement: Hadhrat Maulana Mufti Muhammad Yusuf Saheb Tadali (may his shadow be extended), servant of Hadith at Darul Uloom Deoband. Praising and sending blessings, to proceed: Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair is a very famous book of Ibn Nujaym al-Misri and is included in the syllabus of the Ifta course. The respected and honorable Mufti Muhammad Masum Saheb Qasimi has written a commentary in Urdu in a very easy style. God willing, the book will prove beneficial for students. May Allah the Exalted accept the service of the aforementioned and grant him the ability for further services. (Amin, O Lord of the Worlds). Muhammad Yusuf Tadali, servant of Hadith, Darul Uloom Deoband. Endorsement: Maulana Muhammad Shakib Saheb Qasimi, Nazim of Hujjat al-Islam Academy and teacher at Darul Uloom Waqf Deoband. Reflect on the purpose of man's creation. Why was man created? Is earning livelihood the purpose of creation, or was he brought into the world to conquer the universe? Is building lofty skyscrapers and impregnable forts the purpose of his life, or was he created to enjoy the pleasures of this earthly world? The declaration of the Holy Quran is: 'And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me.' When the worship of the Holy God is the purpose of man's creation, then completely achieving this purpose is the guarantee of his salvation. How should man worship and how should he present proof of his servitude in the court of God? Obviously, for this, comprehensive knowledge of the rulings of Shariah is necessary so that he can succeed in his purpose. Consider: one who is unaware of the rulings of Islam, who is unfamiliar with Islamic jurisprudence, whose mind is unacquainted with religious consciousness, how far is he from his purpose in life? Do not only keep in view the aspect of the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, 'Whoever Allah intends good for, He grants him understanding of the religion,' that Allah, the Lord of Might, gives understanding of the religion to whomever He wishes to treat with goodness. Rather, it is also necessary to consider the aspect: what will Allah's treatment be with one who has not acquired understanding of the religion? In short, man cannot fully complete his purpose of creation until he develops a connection with the knowledge of fiqh. Whatever is in the Quran and Hadith regarding the knowledge of fiqh is sufficient to prove the importance of this knowledge. In every era, its importance has been understood, its necessity realized, and people in every age have learned and taught it. The experts of this art dedicated their lives in the early period for the codification of this art, spent their capital, and continued to simplify this great knowledge and present it to the Ummah.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage consists of two endorsements (taqriz) for the Urdu commentary on al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, written by Mufti Muhammad Masum Qasimi. The first endorsement is by Mufti Muhammad Yusuf, a senior hadith scholar at Darul Uloom Deoband. He praises the commentary for its easy style and notes that the original work by Ibn Nujaym is a key text in the Ifta curriculum. The second endorsement, by Maulana Muhammad Shakib Qasimi, elaborates on the purpose of human creation (worship) and the necessity of fiqh (Islamic jurisprudence) to achieve that purpose. He cites the Quranic verse (51:56) and the hadith 'man yuridillahu bihi khayran yufaqqihhu fi al-din' to emphasize that understanding the religion is a sign of divine favor and essential for salvation. Both endorsements highlight the importance of the commentary for students of ifta.

Key Terms
تقريظ (taqriz): A written endorsement or appreciation of a book, usually by a respected scholar.
الاشباہ والنظائر (al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair): A classical Hanafi work on legal maxims and similar cases by Zayn al-Din Ibn Nujaym al-Misri.
افتاء (ifta): The process of issuing legal verdicts (fatwas) based on Islamic jurisprudence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the primary function of a taqriz in the Hanafi tradition as seen in this passage?
A) To provide a summary of the book's contents.
B) To endorse the book's reliability and pedagogical value.
C) To critique the book's methodology.
D) To market the book to a general audience.

Key Takeaway
A taqriz is a scholarly endorsement that validates a text's authority and pedagogical suitability within the Hanafi tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Fiqh as the Path to Fulfilling Creation's Purpose
Theological argument for the necessity of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain, citing Quran and Hadith, why the Hanafi school considers fiqh essential for fulfilling the purpose of human creation.

Core Idea
Worship is the purpose of creation, and fiqh is the tool to perform worship correctly, making it indispensable for salvation.

The second endorsement by Maulana Muhammad Shakib Qasimi provides a theological foundation for studying fiqh. It cites the Quranic verse that the purpose of jinn and humankind is worship, and the hadith that understanding religion is a sign of divine goodness. This lesson unpacks that argument and shows how it undergirds the Hanafi emphasis on fiqh education.

Guided Path
1
State the purpose of creation per Quran
The Quran states in Surah al-Dhariyat (51:56): 'I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me.' This is the primary purpose.
The verse is cited in the second endorsement.
2
Explain the hadith about understanding religion
The Prophet (pbuh) said: 'Whoever Allah intends good for, He grants him understanding of the religion (yufaqqihhu fi al-din).' This hadith links divine favor to fiqh knowledge.
The endorsement uses this hadith to argue the necessity of fiqh.
3
Identify the link between worship and fiqh
Worship requires knowledge of how to perform it correctly; fiqh provides the rulings and conditions for valid worship.
Without fiqh, worship may be deficient or invalid.
4
Recognize the consequence of ignorance
The endorser warns that one who is ignorant of fiqh is far from the purpose of life, and perhaps subject to divine displeasure.
The reverse of the hadith is implied: lack of understanding is a sign of being deprived of good.
5
Apply to the Hanafi curriculum
This explains why works like al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair are taught in Ifta: they equip muftis with the jurisprudential knowledge to guide others in worship.
The commentary serves to make fiqh accessible.

Commentary
This passage consists of two endorsements (taqriz) for the Urdu commentary on al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, written by Mufti Muhammad Masum Qasimi. The first endorsement is by Mufti Muhammad Yusuf, a senior hadith scholar at Darul Uloom Deoband. He praises the commentary for its easy style and notes that the original work by Ibn Nujaym is a key text in the Ifta curriculum. The second endorsement, by Maulana Muhammad Shakib Qasimi, elaborates on the purpose of human creation (worship) and the necessity of fiqh (Islamic jurisprudence) to achieve that purpose. He cites the Quranic verse (51:56) and the hadith 'man yuridillahu bihi khayran yufaqqihhu fi al-din' to emphasize that understanding the religion is a sign of divine favor and essential for salvation. Both endorsements highlight the importance of the commentary for students of ifta.

Key Terms
تقريظ (taqriz): A written endorsement or appreciation of a book, usually by a respected scholar.
الاشباہ والنظائر (al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair): A classical Hanafi work on legal maxims and similar cases by Zayn al-Din Ibn Nujaym al-Misri.
افتاء (ifta): The process of issuing legal verdicts (fatwas) based on Islamic jurisprudence.
علم فقہ (ilm al-fiqh): The knowledge of Islamic jurisprudence, covering rulings derived from detailed evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second endorsement, what is the relationship between the purpose of creation and the study of fiqh?
A) Fiqh is only for scholars, not for ordinary worshippers.
B) Fiqh is necessary to perform worship correctly, thereby fulfilling the purpose of creation.
C) Fiqh is optional for those who are sincere.
D) The purpose of creation is independent of fiqh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that fiqh is indispensable because worship is the purpose of creation, and fiqh provides the knowledge to worship correctly.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Purpose of Creation and the Necessity of Fiqh
Taqriz explaining the purpose of creation and the importance of fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Quranic purpose of human creation and argue why comprehensive knowledge of fiqh is essential for fulfilling that purpose.

Core Idea
Worship of Allah is the purpose of creation; fiqh is the roadmap to worship correctly.

The taqriz opens with a profound question: Why were we created? It answers with the Quranic verse that worship is the sole purpose. But how can we worship correctly without knowing the rules? This lesson explores the vital link between the purpose of creation and the study of fiqh, and introduces the commentary Sharh al-Nazair as a tool for mastering Hanafi legal maxims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of creation from the Quran
Recall the verse quoted: 'I did not create jinn and mankind except to worship Me.' This establishes worship as the ultimate goal.
Quran 51:56
2
Relate worship to the need for fiqh
Worship requires following divine commands. Without knowledge of fiqh, worship may be invalid or incomplete.
Fiqh provides the practical rulings for all acts of worship.
3
Analyze the hadith on tafaqquh
The hadith states that Allah intends good for those who gain understanding of the religion. Conversely, lack of understanding may indicate otherwise.
This underscores the importance of studying fiqh.
4
Appreciate the role of this commentary
Sharh al-Nazair simplifies the complex maxims of al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, making them accessible for students and practitioners of ifta.
The commentator Mufti Muhammad Masoom uses simple language and examples.

انسان کی وجہ تخلیق پر غور کیجئے ، انسان کو کیوں پیدا کیا گیا، کیا کسب معاش انسان کا مقصد تخلیق ہے یا تسخیر کائنات کے لئے وہ دنیا میں لایا گیا، اونچی اونچی فلک بوس عمارت اور نا قابل تسخیر قلعے تعمیر کرنا اس کی زندگی کا مقصد ہے یا وہ اس زمین دنیا کی لذتوں سے لطف اندوز ہونے کے لئے پیدا ہوا ہے۔ قرآن حکیم کا اعلان یہ ہے وَمَا خَلَقْتُ الْجِنَّ وَالإِنْسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونَ“ جب خدا وند قدوس کی عبادت ہی انسان کا مقصد تخلیق ٹھہرا تو پھر اس مقصد کو مکمل طور پر حاصل کر لینا ہی انسان کی نجات کا ضامن ہے۔ انسان عبادت کیسے کرے اور اپنی بندگی کا ثبوت بارگاہ خداوندی میں کیسے پیش کرے؟ ظاہر ہے اس کے لئے احکام شریعت کا بھر پور علم ضروری ہے تا کہ وہ اپنے مقصد میں کامیاب وکامران ہو سکے۔ اندازہ کیجئے جو اسلام کے احکام سے بے خبر ہو، جو فقہ اسلامی سے نا آشنا ہو، جس کا ذہن دینی شعور سے نابلد ہو وہ اپنے مقصد زندگی سے کتنا دور ہے؟ حدیث رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم "من يرد الله به خيراً يفقه في الدين" کے صرف اس پہلو کو پیش نظر مت رکھئے کہ اللہ رب العزت جس کے ساتھ بھلائی کا معاملہ کرنا چاہتے ہیں، اسے دین کی سمجھ عطا کر دیتے ہیں بلکہ اس پہلو پر بھی نظر رہنا ضروری ہے کہ جس نے دین کی سمجھ نہیں حاصل کی تو اللہ تعالی کا اس کے ساتھ کیسا معاملہ ہو گا ؟ غرض یہ کہ انسان اپنے مقصد تخلیق کی تکمیل اس وقت تک کامل طور نہیں کر سکتا جب تک وہ علم فقہ سے مناسبت نہ پیدا کر لے۔ علم فقہ کے تعلق سے قرآن و حدیث میں جو کچھ بھی ہے وہ اس علم کی اہمیت کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے کافی ہے، ہر دور میں اس کی اہمیت کو سمجھا گیا، اس کی ضرورت کو سمجھا گیا اور ہر زمانے میں لوگوں نے اسے سیکھا اور سکھایا ہے۔ اس فن کے ماہرین نے ابتدائی دور میں اس فن کی تدوین کے لئے اپنی زندگیاں وقف کیں، اپنا سرمایہ صرف کیا اور اس عظیم الشان علم کو آسان کر کے امت کو پیش کرتے رہے ۔

مسائل کا مصادر تشریع سے حل پیش کیا اور ایسی بے مثال فقہی خدمات پیش کیں کہ امت مسلمہ ان کے بھی احسانات ہر دور کے فقہاء نے اپنی علمی بصیرت ، تفقہ فی الدین اور کتاب وسنت پر اپنی یکساں نظر کی بنا پر اپنے دور کے بعد ہے سے ہمیشہ گراں بار ر ہے گی ۔

زیر نظر کتاب "شرح النظائر الاشباہ والنظائر کی ایک اردو شرح ہے۔ الاشباہ والنظائر عموما مدارس میں تکمیل افتاء کے نصاب میں شامل ہے۔ یہ شرح کئی ایک خصوصیات کی وجہ سے دیگر شروحات سے ممتاز ہے۔ شارح محترم جناب حضرت مولانا مفتی محمد معصوم صاحب نے عبارات کا ہل ترجمہ کیا ہے جو کافی حد تک معنی خیز ہے۔ دوران تشریح شارح نے اس پہلو کو بھی ملحوظ رکھا ہے کہ مسئلہ کی تفہیم آسان سے آسان اسلوب میں ہوتا کہ قاری کی دلچسپی برقرارر ہے، چوں کہ شارح خود بھی ایک با صلاحیت، ذی استعداد اور صاحب علم ہونے کے ساتھ تدریس کا عمدہ تجربہ رکھتے ہیں، اس لئے انہوں نے طلبہ کی طبیعت اور اُن کے ذوق کو ملحوظ رکھتے ہوئے افہام وتفہیم کے لئے سادہ اسلوب اور سہل مثالوں کا استعمال کیا ہے۔ دعا ہے کہ اس کتاب کوعند اللہ اور عند الناس مقبولیت حاصل ہو اور طلبہ و اساتذہ کے لئے یکساں مفید ثابت ہو۔ (آمین)
محمد شکیب قاسمی
ناظم حجتہ الاسلام اکیڈمی
و استاذ دار العلوم وقف دیوبند
Taqriz. Janab Maulana Muhammad Shakeeb Qasimi, Nazim Hujjat al-Islam Academy and Teacher of Darul Uloom Waqf Deoband: Consider the reason for creation of man, why was man created? Is the acquisition of livelihood the purpose of creation, or was he brought to the world to conquer the universe? Is building high skyscrapers and impregnable fortresses the aim of his life, or was he created to enjoy the pleasures of this world? The declaration of the Wise Qur'an is: "And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me." When the worship of the Holy Lord is the purpose of creation, then completely achieving this purpose is the guarantee of human salvation. How should man worship and how should he present proof of his servitude in the Divine court? Obviously, for this, comprehensive knowledge of the commands of Shariah is necessary so that he can be successful in his purpose. Estimate how far is he who is unaware of the commands of Islam, unfamiliar with Islamic fiqh, and whose mind is devoid of religious consciousness from his purpose in life? Do not only consider this aspect of the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, "Whoever Allah intends good for, He gives him understanding of the religion": that Allah, the Lord of Majesty, with whom He wishes to deal well, grants him understanding of the religion; rather, it is also necessary to consider this aspect: what will be Allah's dealing with the one who did not acquire understanding of the religion? In short, man cannot completely fulfill his purpose of creation until he establishes a connection with the knowledge of fiqh. Whatever is in the Qur'an and hadith regarding the knowledge of fiqh is sufficient to prove the importance of this knowledge. In every era, its importance was understood, its need was understood, and in every time people learned and taught it. The experts of this art devoted their lives in the early period for the compilation of this art, spent their capital, and continued to present this great knowledge to the Ummah by making it easy. They presented solutions to issues from the sources of legislation, and presented such unparalleled fiqhi services that the Muslim Ummah will always remain indebted for their favors. The jurists of every era, based on their intellectual insight, understanding of the religion (tafaquh fi al-din), and their equal consideration of the Book and Sunnah, are later than their time. The book under consideration, "Sharh al-Nazair," is an Urdu commentary of al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair. Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair is generally included in the curriculum of completion of ifta in madrasas. This commentary is distinguished from other commentaries due to several features. The respected commentator, Hazrat Maulana Mufti Muhammad Masoom Sahib, has provided a complete translation of the phrases, which is quite meaningful. During the commentary, the commentator has also kept in view that the understanding of the issue should be in the easiest possible style so that the reader's interest remains sustained. Since the commentator himself is capable, talented, knowledgeable, and has excellent teaching experience, therefore, keeping in view the nature and taste of the students, he has used simple style and easy examples for understanding and comprehension. Prayer that this book may gain acceptance from Allah and among the people, and prove equally beneficial for students and teachers. (Ameen). Muhammad Shakeeb Qasimi, Nazim Hujjat al-Islam Academy, and Teacher of Darul Uloom Waqf Deoband.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a taqriz (appreciation) written by Maulana Muhammad Shakeeb Qasimi for the book 'Sharh al-Nazair', an Urdu commentary on 'Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair'. The author begins by reflecting on the purpose of human creation, citing the Quranic verse that mankind and jinn were created only to worship Allah. He argues that fulfilling this purpose requires a deep understanding of Islamic law (fiqh), as without it, one cannot worship correctly. He emphasizes the importance of tafaqquh fi al-din (understanding of religion) based on the hadith, warning that those lacking such understanding may face divine displeasure. He praises the early jurists for their efforts in codifying fiqh and making it accessible. The passage then introduces the commentary, noting its inclusion in the ifta curriculum and highlighting its features: the translator/commentator, Maulana Mufti Muhammad Masoom, has provided a complete and meaningful translation, used simple language and examples to maintain reader interest, and drawn on his own teaching experience. The taqriz concludes with a prayer for the book's acceptance and usefulness.

Key Terms
الاشباہ والنظائر (al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair): The well-known work on Hanafi legal maxims and similar cases, authored by Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym.
فقہ (fiqh): Islamic jurisprudence; understanding and knowledge of the practical rulings of Shariah derived from detailed evidence.

What is the main reason the author emphasizes the study of fiqh?
A) To earn a living as a scholar.
B) To properly worship Allah.
C) To debate with non-Muslims.
D) To become a mufti.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of fiqh is indispensable for authentic worship and fulfilling the purpose of creation.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Importance of Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair for Fatwa
Author's preface explaining the book's importance and his facilitation method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the significance of Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair in Hanafi fatwa methodology and explain the author’s approach to facilitating its study.

Core Idea
Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair is the encyclopedia of Hanafi legal maxims—master it, and fatwa becomes systematic rather than guesswork.

This lesson introduces you to the preface of an Urdu commentary on Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, a cornerstone work on Hanafi legal maxims. The author, Muhammad Masum Qasimi, explains why this book is essential for anyone undertaking the responsibility of ifta (issuing fatwas) and shares the method he used to make it more accessible. Understanding this preface will help you appreciate the purpose and structure of the commentary that follows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Book and Its Status
Recognize that Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair is described as an 'encyclopedia of Islamic jurisprudence' for its systematic compilation of legal maxims and analogous cases.
The book is part of the official curriculum for ifta in many seminaries.
2
Recognize the Core Message: Why Students Struggle
Note the author's lament that students do not give this book due attention, leading to errors in fatwa practice. The key takeaway: understanding maxims reduces the burden of memorizing every single case.
The maxims are few, but their applications are many.
3
Analyze the Author's Methodology
The author lists his facilitations: diacritical marks for correct reading, literal plus idiomatic translation, simple explanation, and avoidance of unnecessary detail.
This approach aims to benefit students of average ability.
4
Connect to Fatwa Practice
Recognize the link between mastering maxims and competent fatwa: a mufti who knows the maxims can derive rulings for new cases efficiently and accurately.
Errors often occur when a mufti does not ground his ruling in the relevant qawida.

محمد معصوم مظفر نگری
خویدم جامعة المؤمنين منگلور ضلع ہریدوار اتراکھنڈ ا نڈیا
Preface
Muhammad Masum Qasimi Muzaffarnagari
Servant of Hadith, Jamia al-Mu'minin, Manglore, District Haridwar, Uttarakhand, India
On the derivation of issues from legal maxims and the application and explanation of each maxim in terms of numerous similarities and details, if Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair is called an encyclopedia of Islamic jurisprudence, it would not be an exaggeration. This magnificent book is included in the curriculum of ifta in central religious seminaries and is of great importance and benefit. If ifta students study this book with attention and interest, then surely they will face no difficulty in clarifying the legal ruling for new and varied issues and in deriving numerous issues by the light of one maxim. But it must be said with regret that students do not show the interest towards such a capacity-building and important book that it deserves. The result is obvious: in carrying out the delicate and sensitive responsibility of ifta, one faces difficulty at every step, and sometimes such grave mistakes occur that even the public, let alone the elite, begin to criticize them. Therefore, it is necessary that students who enroll in a dar al-ifta should study Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair with special attention along with other books of ifta. If a maxim or a derived analogue is not understood, they should resolve it before proceeding further. In truth, this delay is not necessary because in Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair the maxims are not many; however, for the explanation and detail of whatever maxims are mentioned, there are so many examples and analogues that memorizing them sometimes becomes difficult. The writer, considering the importance of the book, had been desirous of its facilitation and dissemination for a long time. It is purely the grace of Allah, the Lord of Might, that He enabled this lowly person to accomplish the work despite various engagements and responsibilities. Accordingly, the method I have adopted for the explanation and facilitation of this book is as follows: The correct wording along with diacritical marks has been ensured so that no difficulty arises in the text itself. 
"Alif Lam"
Under the word
Sufficiency has been made. 
Both literal and idiomatic translation have been taken into account so that understanding becomes easy. Explanation has been done in a simple and easy style so that students of average ability can also benefit. The book itself is lengthy, so avoiding unnecessary discussions, explanations have been given as needed. At the end, I am grateful to my noble teacher, Khatib al-Islam, Hazrat Maulana Muhammad Salim Sahib Qasimi (may his blessings endure), Chairman of Darul Uloom Waqf Deoband; my revered respected teacher, Hazrat Maulana Mufti Ghulam Nabi Sahib, teacher of Hadith at Darul Uloom Waqf Deoband; Hazrat Maulana Abdur Rashid Sahib Bastavi, teacher at Jamia Imam Muhammad Anwar Shah Deoband; Maulana Muhammad Shamsad Sahib Rahmani, teacher at Darul Uloom Waqf Deoband; Hazrat Maulana Shakib Ahmad Sahib, grandson of Hakim al-Islam and manager of Hujjat al-Islam Academy; Hazrat Maulana Muhammad Yusuf Sahib, teacher at Darul Uloom Deoband and author of many books, for increasing the value of the book through their valuable and blessed remarks and for encouraging this lowly one. May Allah keep the shade of their affection, health, and safety, and continue their academic grace (Ameen). I am also grateful to those from whose books and commentaries I have benefited. Also to my dear Mufti Muhammad Tawfiq Sahib, teacher at Jamia al-Mu'minin Mangalur, and Bashir Sahib, teacher at Darul Uloom Arshad Jawalapur, whose advice gave rise to the motivation to write this commentary. It would be ungrateful if I do not mention Hazrat Maulana Mufti Azimuddin Sahib Faizabadi, teacher at Darul Uloom al-Asr, who performed the duties of proofreading and made the benefit of the book easiest and simplest. Every effort has been made, yet if any error remains in the book or in the edition, Insha Allah it will be corrected in the next edition. Finally, I request all readers to remember this humble one, my parents, and my esteemed teachers in good supplications.
Muhammad Masum Muzaffarnagari,
Servant of Jamia al-Mu'minin Manglore, District Haridwar, Uttarakhand, India.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This is the author's preface to his Urdu commentary on Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair. He begins by emphasizing the critical importance of this work for students of ifta (fatwa issuance), describing it as an encyclopedia of Islamic jurisprudence. He laments that students often do not give it the attention it deserves, leading to errors in fatwa practice. He urges students to study it thoroughly and resolve any difficulties before moving on. The author then explains his methodology: he has included diacritical marks for correct reading, provided both literal and idiomatic translations, and used simple language for easy comprehension. He also acknowledges his teachers and benefactors who contributed to the work. The preface serves as a motivational and methodological introduction, setting the stage for the commentary that follows.

Key Terms
الاشباہ والنظائر (al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair): Title of a seminal work on Hanafi legal maxims and their applications, authored by Zain al-Din ibn Nujaym. The book compiles similar cases and analogous rulings under legal maxims.
قواعد فقہیہ (qawaid fiqhiyya): Legal maxims; general principles of Islamic jurisprudence from which multiple specific rulings are derived. In this context, the author refers to the maxims presented in Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair.

Understanding Nadb in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines the legal category of nadb in Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define nadb, distinguish it from mubah and wajib, and apply the definition to classify an act as recommended.

Core Idea
Nadb: reward for doing, no sin for leaving — it is not the same as mubah.

This lesson defines the Hanafi legal category of nadb (recommended). Understanding this category is essential for distinguishing between obligatory, recommended, and neutral acts. The definition hinges on reward and sin: doing is preferable and rewarded, leaving is permissible but without reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its genus
The passage defines 'nadb' as a category of actions. Start by isolating the term being defined.
2
Note the permissible dichotomy
Both doing and leaving are legally permissible (ja'iz). This distinguishes nadb from wajib (where leaving is not permissible).
Permissibility does not mean equal reward.
3
Identify the preference (rujhan)
The doer's action is 'rajih' (preferable) while leaving the action is 'marjuh' (less preferable). This preference is the basis for reward.
4
Understand the consequence
Performing the act brings reward; leaving it brings no sin. This is the operative effect (athar) of nadb.
5
Compare with adjacent categories
Contrast nadb with mubah (equal, no reward) and wajib (sinful to leave). This clarifies the boundaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ندب کی تعریف: جس میں فعل اور ترک فعل دونوں جائز ہوں مگر فعل (کرنے) راج اور ترک فعل مرجوح ہو۔
Definition of Nadb: That in which both the doing and leaving of the action are permissible, but the doing (of the doer) is preferable and the leaving of the action is less preferable.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage defines the category of nadb (recommended) in Hanafi fiqh. It explains that in nadb, both performing and leaving the act are legally permissible, but performing it carries greater reward and is thus preferable, while leaving it is less rewardable but not sinful. This distinguishes nadb from wajib (where leaving is sinful) and from mubah (where both are equal).

Key Terms
ندب (nadb): An act whose performance is preferable but not obligatory, and whose omission is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling on leaving a nadb (recommended) act?
A) It is sinful
B) It is permissible but less rewardable
C) It is obligatory to make up (qada)
D) It is forbidden

Key Takeaway
Nadb is a recommended act: doing it earns reward, leaving it is not sinful.

Linguistic and Terminological Meaning of Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir
Explains the linguistic roots and technical definition of the book title

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and terminological definitions of Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir and distinguish it from other genres.

Core Idea
Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir are synonyms in language but in fiqh they refer to seemingly similar cases with hidden differences leading to different rulings.

This lesson introduces the foundational work of Hanafi legal maxims. Understanding its title is key to appreciating the genre: collecting cases that look alike but rule differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic root
Shabah means similarity, and both al-ashbah and al-naza'ir are plurals meaning similar things.
Both words share the same basic meaning in Arabic.
2
Understand the linguistic synonymy
Linguistically, the two words are synonyms, both meaning 'similarities' or 'resemblances'.
Some scholars use them interchangeably.
3
Grasp the terminological shift
In technical Hanafi usage, the phrase refers to cases that appear similar but have different rulings due to hidden reasons.
This distinction is the core of the genre.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاشباہ والنظائر کی لغوی تحقیق: الاشباہ شَبَہ کی جمع ہے جس کے معنی مثل کے ہیں۔ النظائر نظیر کی جمع ہے اس کے معنی بھی مثل کے ہیں۔ لغت کے اعتبار سے الاشباہ والنظائر مترادف ہیں۔ اصطلاحی تعریف: الاشباہ والنظائر ان مسائل کو کہتے ہیں جو بظاہر ایک دوسرے جیسے معلوم ہوتے ہیں لیکن بعض امور خفیہ کی وجہ سے ان میں فرق ہوتا ہے۔
Linguistic research of Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir: Al-Ashbah is the plural of Shabah, which means similar. Al-Naza'ir is the plural of Nazir, which also means similar. Linguistically, Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir are synonyms. Terminological definition: Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir refers to those issues that seemingly resemble each other, but due to some hidden matters, there is a difference between them.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage clarifies the meaning of the title Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. Linguistically, both words mean 'similar things' and are synonyms. In technical usage, the term refers to a genre of fiqh literature that collects legal issues that appear similar but have different rulings due to subtle underlying reasons. This book is a foundational work in the Hanafi science of legal maxims and similar cases.

Key Terms
الاشباہ (al-ashbah): Plural of shabah, meaning similar things or resemblances.
النظائر (al-naza'ir): Plural of nazir, meaning analogues or counterparts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir refers to a genre of Hanafi fiqh that examines cases appearing similar but ruling differently due to hidden distinctions.

Reconciling Hadiths: The Principle of Jam' in Hanafi Methodology
Objection and answer on reconciling basmalah and hamd hadiths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of combining (jam') to reconcile two apparently conflicting hadiths by distinguishing between real and relative beginnings.

Core Idea
Combine contradictory texts before preferring—distinguish real vs. relative application.

The mufti often faces texts that seem contradictory. Hanafi methodology teaches to reconcile by specifying contexts. This lesson demonstrates how two hadiths on beginning actions with Allah's name can both be followed through the principle of jam'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two hadiths
Locate the hadith of basmalah and the hadith of hamd (tahmid) as cited in the passage. Both are about beginning important matters.
The basmalah hadith is 'Every matter of importance not begun with the remembrance of Allah is cut off.' The hamd hadith is implied in the objection.
2
Recognize the apparent conflict
The conflict arises because one hadith commands beginning with basmalah, the other with hamd. Acting on one seems to neglect the other.
The objection in the passage states this.
3
Apply the Hanafi method of jam'
Combine the two hadiths by interpreting each as referring to a different type of beginning: real (haqiqi) for basmalah, and relative or customary (idafi/urfi) for hamd.
The passage offers two ways: real vs. relative, or real vs. customary.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The justification is that 'Allah' indicates the essence, and 'hamd' indicates an attribute; the essence precedes the attribute. Thus basmalah marks the real start.
This is a theological principle applied to hadith reconciliation.
5
Note the function of the ba in bismillah
The ba can be for isti'anah (seeking help) or tabarruk (blessing). This further clarifies the pragmatic use of basmalah.
Not directly part of reconciliation, but contextually relevant.

Source Text

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
ترجمه شروع کرتا ہوں اللہ کے نام سے جو بے حد مہربان اور نہا یت رحم کرنے والا ہے۔ تشریح علامہ ابن قیم المصری علیہ الرحمہ نے اپنی کتاب الاشباہ والنظائر کا آغاز اللہ کی کتاب قرآن مقدس کی اقتداء اور نبی اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی حدیث "کل امر ذی بال لا يبدا فيه بذكر الله وببسم الله فهو أقطع" پر عمل کرتے ہوئے بسملہ اور حمد لہ سے کیا ہے۔
اعتراض : حدیث بسملہ اور حدیث حملہ میں بظاہر تعارض ہے ایک پر عمل کرنے سے دوسرے پر عمل فوت ہو جاتا ہے۔
جواب: اس کا یہ ہے کہ دونوں کو جمع کرنا ممکن ہے اس طریقہ پر کہ حدیث بسملہ کو ابتدائے حقیقی پر اور حد بیٹے حملہ کو ابتدائے اضافی پرمحمول کر لیا جائے یا حدیثہ بسملہ کو ابتدائے حقیقی پر اور حد بیت عدلیہ کو ابتدائے عرفی پر۔ حدیث بسملہ کو ابتدائے حقیقی پر حمل کرنے کی وجہ بظاہر یہ ہو سکتی ہے کہ اللہ ذات پر دلیل ہے اور حمد صفت پر اور ذات صفت پر مقدم ہوا کرتی ہے۔
باب بسم اللہ میں یا تو استعانت کے لئے ہے یا تبرک کے لئے۔ الله: یہ ذات باری تعالیٰ کا علم ہے اور مختار قول اللہ کے غیر مشتق ہونے کا ہے خلیل نحوی ، امام سید و سیا کثر اصولیین اور فقہاء اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اللہ نام ہے اس ذات واجب الوجود کا جس کے اندر جملہ صفات کمالیہ ہوں اور نقص اور علامت نقص سے پاک ہو۔ لفظ اللہ جملہ اسماء کا امام ہے۔ اللہ کے علاوہ کسی اور پر اس کا اطلاق ممنوع ہے اللہ نے اس نام کو اپنی ذات اقدس کے ساتھ مختص کر دیا اور آج تک کوئی اپنا نام اللہ نہ رکھ سکا، بعض مشرکین نے اپنے کسی بت کا نا رکھنا چاہا تھا لیکن اللہ نے بجائے لفظ اللہ کے لات کی طرف ان کے ذہن کو پھیر دیا۔ الرحمن الرحيم: قعلان کے وزن پر رحم سے مشتق ہے جیسے غضبان غضب سے مشتق ہے اور رحیم فعیل کے وزن پر رحم سے ہی مشتق ہے ، رحمان میں رحیم کے مقابلہ میں مبالغہ زیادہ ہے اسی وجہ سے علماء کہتے ہیں "رحمان الدنيا والآخره ورحيم الدنيا" نیز حروف کی زیادتی معنی کی زیادتی پر دلالت کرتی ہے رحمان میں حروف زیادہ ہیں یہ نسبت رحیم کے۔ اللہ کو رحمت کے ساتھ متصف کرنے کے معنی ہیں افاضہ خیر اور رحیم کا ذکر رحمن کے بعد تمیم اور ردیف کے ینے سے وجہسے مجرور ہیں جن قبیل سے ہے رحمن ورحیم اللہ کی صفت ہونے کی وجہ سے مجرور ہیں اور صفات مادحہ میں سے ہیں جن کا مقصد اللہ کی
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. I begin the translation with the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Explanation: Allamah Ibn Qayyim al-Misri (may Allah have mercy on him) began his book Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir with basmalah and tahmid, following the Book of Allah, the Holy Quran, and the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ): "Every matter of importance that is not begun with the remembrance of Allah and with bismillah is cut off." Objection: There is apparent contradiction between the hadith of basmalah and the hadith of tahmid; acting on one causes neglect of the other. Answer: It is possible to combine both by interpreting the hadith of basmalah as referring to a real beginning and the hadith of tahmid as referring to a relative beginning, or the hadith of basmalah as a real beginning and the hadith of hamd as a customary beginning. The reason for interpreting the basmalah hadith as real beginning is that 'Allah' indicates the essence and 'hamd' indicates the attribute, and the essence precedes the attribute. The ba in bismillah is either for seeking help (isti'anah) or for blessing (tabarruk). Allah: This is the proper name of the Divine Essence, and the chosen view is that Allah is non-derived (ghayr mushtaq); Khalil al-Nahwi, Imam Sayyid [?], and many usuliyyun and fuqaha hold this view. 'Allah' is the name of that Necessary Being who possesses all perfect attributes and is free from deficiency and any sign of deficiency. The word 'Allah' is the chief of all names. Its application to anyone else is prohibited; Allah has reserved this name for His holy essence, and no one has been able to name themselves Allah. Some polytheists wanted to name an idol with it, but Allah diverted their minds to 'Al-Lat' instead. Al-Rahman al-Rahim: Both are derived from 'rahmah' (mercy); 'Rahman' is on the pattern of fa'lan, like ghadban from ghadab, and 'Rahim' is on the pattern of fa'il, also from rahmah. 'Rahman' indicates greater intensity than 'Rahim'; therefore scholars say "Rahman of this world and the Hereafter, and Rahim of this world." Also, increase in letters indicates increase in meaning; 'Rahman' has more letters in comparison to 'Rahim'. The meaning of attributing mercy to Allah is the bestowal of good. And 'Rahim' is mentioned after 'Rahman' as following and accompaniment; both are in the genitive case because they are attributes of Allah and are among the attributes of praise whose purpose is of Allah...
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an excerpt from the commentary's introduction explaining why the author began with basmalah and hamd. The author (stated as Allamah Ibn Qayyim al-Misri, though the book is usually by Ibn Nujaym, so this appears to be a misattribution in the commentary, but we stick to the text) begins with basmalah following Quranic precedent and a hadith that any important matter not begun with Allah's name is cut off. An objection is raised that there are two hadiths—one about basmalah, another about hamd—which seem contradictory since one begins with basmalah and the other with hamd. The answer is to reconcile them by distinguishing between a real beginning (basmalah) and a relative or customary beginning (hamd). The ba in bismillah indicates either seeking help (isti'anah) or blessing (tabarruk). Then the text delves into the meaning of 'Allah', stating it is a proper name (alam), non-derived, and exclusive to God. It then discusses 'Rahman' and 'Rahim': both derived from mercy, but 'Rahman' has greater intensity (mubalaghah), covering both worlds, while 'Rahim' is more specific to this world. The increase in letters indicates increase in meaning. The passage ends discussing the grammar: both are adjectives, thus genitive, and are attributes of praise.

Key Terms
الله (Allah): The proper name (alam) of the Divine Essence, non-derived, applied exclusively to the Necessary Being with all perfect attributes.
الرحمن (al-Rahman): Derived from rahmah, on the pattern fa'lan, indicating intensity; refers to mercy encompassing both this world and the Hereafter.
الرحيم (al-Rahim): Derived from rahmah, on the pattern fa'il, indicating mercy; in this passage, it is said to be specific to this world.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Hanafi methodology prioritizes combining (jam') conflicting texts by distinguishing their application contexts before resorting to preference (tarjih).

Linguistic Principles in Divine Names: Derivation and Indication
Linguistic analysis of the divine names in the basmalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi view on the derivation (ishtiqaq) of the names Allah, Rahman, and Rahim, and apply the principle that increase in letters indicates increase in meaning.

Core Idea
Allah is non-derived and exclusive; Rahman and Rahim derive from mercy, with Rahman conveying greater intensity due to its longer form.

The names of Allah in the basmalah are not mere titles; they carry linguistic weight that affects legal interpretation. Understanding their derivation and intensity helps the mufti discern the intended meaning in oaths, contracts, and devotional acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three names discussed
The passage names Allah, al-Rahman, and al-Rahim. Note that they are in the genitive case because they are attributes of Allah.
The grammatical case is important for Arabic parsing (i'rab).
2
Determine the status of 'Allah' regarding derivation
The passage states that the chosen view is that Allah is non-derived (ghayr mushtaq), i.e., a proper name not taken from any root. Supporters include Khalil al-Nahwi and many usuliyyun.
Some grammarians derive it from 'ilah'; Hanafis reject this.
3
Analyze the derivation of 'Rahman' and 'Rahim'
Both are derived from 'rahmah' (mercy). 'Rahman' is on the pattern fa'lan indicating intensity (like ghadban); 'Rahim' is on fa'il indicating a more specific or lesser intensity.
The pattern fa'lan in Arabic often denotes heightened intensity or episodic states.
4
Apply the principle of letter increase indicating meaning increase
The passage explicitly states: 'increase in letters indicates increase in meaning.' Since 'Rahman' has more letters than 'Rahim', it indicates greater mercy, encompassing both worlds, while 'Rahim' is specific to this world.
This is a recognized linguistic principle used in fiqh to derive nuances.
5
Note the exclusive application of 'Allah'
Allah is exclusive to the Divine Essence; no creation can bear this name. The passage mentions that polytheists tried to name an idol 'Allah' but were diverted to 'Al-Lat'.
This has legal implications, e.g., for the validity of oaths and for tawheed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
ترجمه شروع کرتا ہوں اللہ کے نام سے جو بے حد مہربان اور نہا یت رحم کرنے والا ہے۔ تشریح علامہ ابن قیم المصری علیہ الرحمہ نے اپنی کتاب الاشباہ والنظائر کا آغاز اللہ کی کتاب قرآن مقدس کی اقتداء اور نبی اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی حدیث "کل امر ذی بال لا يبدا فيه بذكر الله وببسم الله فهو أقطع" پر عمل کرتے ہوئے بسملہ اور حمد لہ سے کیا ہے۔
اعتراض : حدیث بسملہ اور حدیث حملہ میں بظاہر تعارض ہے ایک پر عمل کرنے سے دوسرے پر عمل فوت ہو جاتا ہے۔
جواب: اس کا یہ ہے کہ دونوں کو جمع کرنا ممکن ہے اس طریقہ پر کہ حدیث بسملہ کو ابتدائے حقیقی پر اور حد بیٹے حملہ کو ابتدائے اضافی پرمحمول کر لیا جائے یا حدیثہ بسملہ کو ابتدائے حقیقی پر اور حد بیت عدلیہ کو ابتدائے عرفی پر۔ حدیث بسملہ کو ابتدائے حقیقی پر حمل کرنے کی وجہ بظاہر یہ ہو سکتی ہے کہ اللہ ذات پر دلیل ہے اور حمد صفت پر اور ذات صفت پر مقدم ہوا کرتی ہے۔
باب بسم اللہ میں یا تو استعانت کے لئے ہے یا تبرک کے لئے۔ الله: یہ ذات باری تعالیٰ کا علم ہے اور مختار قول اللہ کے غیر مشتق ہونے کا ہے خلیل نحوی ، امام سید و سیا کثر اصولیین اور فقہاء اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اللہ نام ہے اس ذات واجب الوجود کا جس کے اندر جملہ صفات کمالیہ ہوں اور نقص اور علامت نقص سے پاک ہو۔ لفظ اللہ جملہ اسماء کا امام ہے۔ اللہ کے علاوہ کسی اور پر اس کا اطلاق ممنوع ہے اللہ نے اس نام کو اپنی ذات اقدس کے ساتھ مختص کر دیا اور آج تک کوئی اپنا نام اللہ نہ رکھ سکا، بعض مشرکین نے اپنے کسی بت کا نا رکھنا چاہا تھا لیکن اللہ نے بجائے لفظ اللہ کے لات کی طرف ان کے ذہن کو پھیر دیا۔ الرحمن الرحيم: قعلان کے وزن پر رحم سے مشتق ہے جیسے غضبان غضب سے مشتق ہے اور رحیم فعیل کے وزن پر رحم سے ہی مشتق ہے ، رحمان میں رحیم کے مقابلہ میں مبالغہ زیادہ ہے اسی وجہ سے علماء کہتے ہیں "رحمان الدنيا والآخره ورحيم الدنيا" نیز حروف کی زیادتی معنی کی زیادتی پر دلالت کرتی ہے رحمان میں حروف زیادہ ہیں یہ نسبت رحیم کے۔ اللہ کو رحمت کے ساتھ متصف کرنے کے معنی ہیں افاضہ خیر اور رحیم کا ذکر رحمن کے بعد تمیم اور ردیف کے ینے سے وجہسے مجرور ہیں جن قبیل سے ہے رحمن ورحیم اللہ کی صفت ہونے کی وجہ سے مجرور ہیں اور صفات مادحہ میں سے ہیں جن کا مقصد اللہ کی
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. I begin the translation with the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Explanation: Allamah Ibn Qayyim al-Misri (may Allah have mercy on him) began his book Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir with basmalah and tahmid, following the Book of Allah, the Holy Quran, and the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ): "Every matter of importance that is not begun with the remembrance of Allah and with bismillah is cut off." Objection: There is apparent contradiction between the hadith of basmalah and the hadith of tahmid; acting on one causes neglect of the other. Answer: It is possible to combine both by interpreting the hadith of basmalah as referring to a real beginning and the hadith of tahmid as referring to a relative beginning, or the hadith of basmalah as a real beginning and the hadith of hamd as a customary beginning. The reason for interpreting the basmalah hadith as real beginning is that 'Allah' indicates the essence and 'hamd' indicates the attribute, and the essence precedes the attribute. The ba in bismillah is either for seeking help (isti'anah) or for blessing (tabarruk). Allah: This is the proper name of the Divine Essence, and the chosen view is that Allah is non-derived (ghayr mushtaq); Khalil al-Nahwi, Imam Sayyid [?], and many usuliyyun and fuqaha hold this view. 'Allah' is the name of that Necessary Being who possesses all perfect attributes and is free from deficiency and any sign of deficiency. The word 'Allah' is the chief of all names. Its application to anyone else is prohibited; Allah has reserved this name for His holy essence, and no one has been able to name themselves Allah. Some polytheists wanted to name an idol with it, but Allah diverted their minds to 'Al-Lat' instead. Al-Rahman al-Rahim: Both are derived from 'rahmah' (mercy); 'Rahman' is on the pattern of fa'lan, like ghadban from ghadab, and 'Rahim' is on the pattern of fa'il, also from rahmah. 'Rahman' indicates greater intensity than 'Rahim'; therefore scholars say "Rahman of this world and the Hereafter, and Rahim of this world." Also, increase in letters indicates increase in meaning; 'Rahman' has more letters in comparison to 'Rahim'. The meaning of attributing mercy to Allah is the bestowal of good. And 'Rahim' is mentioned after 'Rahman' as following and accompaniment; both are in the genitive case because they are attributes of Allah and are among the attributes of praise whose purpose is of Allah...
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an excerpt from the commentary's introduction explaining why the author began with basmalah and hamd. The author (stated as Allamah Ibn Qayyim al-Misri, though the book is usually by Ibn Nujaym, so this appears to be a misattribution in the commentary, but we stick to the text) begins with basmalah following Quranic precedent and a hadith that any important matter not begun with Allah's name is cut off. An objection is raised that there are two hadiths—one about basmalah, another about hamd—which seem contradictory since one begins with basmalah and the other with hamd. The answer is to reconcile them by distinguishing between a real beginning (basmalah) and a relative or customary beginning (hamd). The ba in bismillah indicates either seeking help (isti'anah) or blessing (tabarruk). Then the text delves into the meaning of 'Allah', stating it is a proper name (alam), non-derived, and exclusive to God. It then discusses 'Rahman' and 'Rahim': both derived from mercy, but 'Rahman' has greater intensity (mubalaghah), covering both worlds, while 'Rahim' is more specific to this world. The increase in letters indicates increase in meaning. The passage ends discussing the grammar: both are adjectives, thus genitive, and are attributes of praise.

Key Terms
الله (Allah): The proper name (alam) of the Divine Essence, non-derived, applied exclusively to the Necessary Being with all perfect attributes.
الرحمن (al-Rahman): Derived from rahmah, on the pattern fa'lan, indicating intensity; refers to mercy encompassing both this world and the Hereafter.
الرحيم (al-Rahim): Derived from rahmah, on the pattern fa'il, indicating mercy; in this passage, it is said to be specific to this world.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does 'Rahman' indicate a more extensive mercy than 'Rahim'?
A) Because 'Rahman' appears first in the basmalah.
B) Because 'Rahman' is derived from a different root.
C) Because 'Rahman' has more letters and is on pattern fa'lan, which indicates intensity.
D) Because 'Rahim' is only used for this world while 'Rahman' is for the Hereafter.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses linguistic principles, such as the pattern of Arabic nouns and the rule of letter increase, to derive nuanced understandings of divine names and their legal implications.

Introduction and Front Matter
advanced
8 min
Reconciling Basmalah and Hamd: A Hanafi Linguistic Introduction
Author's introduction with linguistic analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the linguistic devices used by Hanafi scholars to reconcile apparent conflicts in proof texts and define the key divine names with precision.

Core Idea
Apparent conflicts between sacred texts can be resolved by distinguishing real and attributive beginnings.

The author begins by justifying his opening with basmalah and hamd, addressing an apparent contradiction between two hadiths. Using linguistic analysis, he explains the meanings of 'Allah', 'al-Rahman', 'al-Rahim', and the definite article 'al-' in 'al-hamd'. This introduction sets the methodological foundation for Hanafi usul al-iftaa: precision in terms and reconciliation of proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent conflict
The two hadiths (requiring basmalah and hamd) seem to dictate different openings. The objection is that acting on one leads to missing the other.
This is a classic tawarud (contradiction) problem.
2
Apply the author's resolution
The author distinguishes between 'real beginning' (al-ibtida' al-haqiqi) and 'additional/customary beginning' (al-ibtida' al-idafi/al-'urfi). Basmalah is for the real beginning, hamd for the additional one, because Allah's essence (indicated by 'Allah') precedes attributes (indicated by hamd).
This shows the priority of essence over attributes.
3
Analyze the key terms: Allah, Rahman, Rahim
'Allah' is a proper noun, non-derived, and exclusive. 'Rahman' (pattern fa'lan) has greater intensification and applies to both worlds; 'Rahim' (pattern fa'il) applies mainly to this world. The author notes the grammatical debate on the declinability of 'Rahman'.
Increase in letters indicates increase in meaning.
4
Analyze the definite article in 'al-hamd'
The author lists four uses of 'al-': external 'ahd, mental 'ahd, istighraq (comprehensive), and jins (generic). He argues for the generic/comprehensive meaning, and addresses the Mu'tazila view that it is for 'ahd (specific). He then rebuts the objection that this would make praising others invalid, explaining that all praise ultimately returns to Allah.
This demonstrates how linguistic analysis resolves theological-legal objections.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
:ترجمه شروع کرتا ہوں اللہ کے نام سے جو بے حد مہربان اور نہا یت رحم کرنے والا ہے ۔ تشریح علامہ ابن قیم المصری علیہ الرحمہ نے اپنی کتاب الاشباہ والنظائر کا آغاز اللہ کی کتاب قرآن مقدس کی اقتداء اور نبی اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی حدیث کل امر دی بال لا يبدا فيه بذكر الله وببسم الله فهو قطع " پر عمل کرتے ہوئے بسملہ اور حمد لہ سے کیا ہے۔ اعتراض : حدیث بسملہ اور حدیث [حمد؟] میں بظاہر تعارض ہے ایک پر عمل کرنے سے دوسرے پر عمل فوت ہو جاتا ہے۔
جواب: اس کا یہ ہے کہ دونوں کو جمع کرنا ممکن ہے اس طریقہ پر کہ حدیث بسملہ کو ابتدائے حقیقی پر اور حدیث [حمد؟] کو ابتدائے اضافی پرمحمول کر لیا جائے یا حدیث بسملہ کو ابتدائے حقیقی پر اور حدیث [حمد؟] کو ابتدائے عرفی پر۔ حدیث بسملہ کو ابتدائے حقیقی پر حمل کرنے کی وجہ بظاہر یہ ہو سکتی ہے کہ اللہ ذات پر دلیل ہے اور حمد صفت پر اور ذات صفت پر مقدم ہوا کرتی ہے ۔
با بسم اللہ میں یا تو استعانت کے لئے ہے یا تبرک کے لئے ۔ الله: یہ ذات باری تعالیٰ کا علم ہے اور مختار قول اللہ کے غیر مشتق ہونے کا ہے خلیل نحوی ، امام سید و سیا کثر اصولیین اور فقہاء اسی کے قائل ہیں ۔ اللہ نام ہے اس ذات واجب الوجود کا جس کے اندر جملہ صفات کمالیہ ہوں اور نقص اور علامت نقص سے پاک ہو۔ لفظ اللہ جملہ اسماء کا امام ہے۔ اللہ کے علاوہ کسی اور پر اس کا اطلاق ممنوع ہے اللہ نے اس نام کو اپنی ذات اقدس کے ساتھ مختص کر دیا اور آج تک کوئی اپنا نام اللہ نہ رکھ سکا، بعض مشرکین نے اپنے کسی بت کا نا رکھنا چاہا تھا لیکن اللہ نے بجائے لفظ اللہ کے لات کی طرف ان کے ذہن کو پھیر دیا۔ الرحمن الرحيم: قعلان کے وزن پر رحم سے مشتق ہے جیسے غضبان غضب سے مشتق ہے اور رحیم فعیل کے وزن پر رحم سے ہی مشتق ہے ، رحمان میں رحیم کے مقابلہ میں مبالغہ زیادہ ہے اسی وجہ سے علماء کہتے ہیں "رحمان الدنيا والآخره ورحيم الدنيا" نیز حروف کی زیادتی معنی کی زیادتی پر دلالت کرتی ہے رحمان میں حروف زیادہ ہیں یہ نسبت رحیم کے ۔ اللہ کو رحمت کے ساتھ متصف کرنے کے معنی ہیں افاضہ خیر اور رحیم کا ذکر رحمن کے بعد تمیم اور ردیف کے ینے سے وجہسے مجرور ہیں جن قبیل سے ہے رحمن ورحیم اللہ کی صفت ہونے کی وجہ سے مجرور ہیں اور صفات مادحہ میں سے ہیں جن کا مقصد اللہ کی

رحمن کے انصراف اور عدم انصراف میں علماء نحاۃ کا اختلاف بیچنہوں نے منع غیر منصرف کے لئے انتظار فعانہ کو شرط قرار دیا ہے ان کے نزدیک رحمن منع غیر منصرف ہے اور جنہوں نے وجود تعلی کو ضروری قرار دیا ہے ان کے نزدیک منصرف ہے۔ الحمد لله على ما أنعم وصلى الله على سَيّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ وَسَلَّم. ترجمه جمله تعریفیں اللہ کے ساتھ خاص ہیں اس کے انعام کرنے پر اور اللہ کی رحمت و سلامتی نازل ہو ہمارے سردار محمد صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر ۔ تشريح: الف لام یا تو وضع کیا گیا ہے (۱) عبد خارجی کے لئے (۲) یا عہد جہنی کے لئے (۳) یا ستغرق کے لئے (۴) یا تعریف جنس کے لئے ۔ لیکن اصل ان میں عہد ہے پھر استغراق پھر تعریف جنس اس لئے کہ وہ لفظ جس پر لام داخل ہو اور وہ ماہیت پر بدون لام دلالت کرے تو وہاں لام کو فائدہ جدیدہ پر محمول کرتا اولی ہے اس کو تعریف طبیعہ پر محمول کرنے سے۔ اور فائدہ جدیدہ یہاں یا تو تعریف عہد میں ہے یا استغراق جنس میں ہے اور تعریف عبد اولی ہے استغراق سے ۔ اس لئے کہ بعض افراد جنس کو عبد خارجی و عہد ذہنی کے اعتبار سے ذکر کیا جائے گا اور ام کو بعض عبد خارجی یا عہد دینی پر محمول کرنا اولی ہے جملہ افراد پر محمول کرنے سے اس لئے کہ بعض متیقن ہے اور کل محتمل ہے پھر علماء میں اختلاف ہوا کہ جب لام مفرد جمع پر داخل ہو۔ تو اہل اصول و عر بیہ کی اکثریت اس کی قائل ہے کہ ان دونوں میں لام استغراق کا فائدہ دے گا مگر جبکہ وہ معبود ہو ابوعلی فارسی کہتے ہیں کہ دونوں صورتوں میں وہ مطلق جنس کے لئے ہوگا نہ کہ استغراق کے لئے اور یہی ابو باشم معتزلی کے دو قولوں میں سے ایک قول ہے اور دوسرا قول ان کا یہ ہے کہ وہ ہے اور دوسراقول یہ ہو مفرد میں مطلق جنس کے لئے ہوگا اور جمع میں مطلق جمع کے لئے نہ کہ استغراق کے لئے مگر کسی دوسری دلیل ہے۔ اور جب تفصیل آپ کو معلوم ہو گئی تو اب سنئے کہ الف لام حمد میں جنس کے لئے ہے یعنی قرینے حمد اللہ کے ساتھ خاص ہے اور دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ الف لام استغراق جنس کے لئے ہے یعنی تمام تعریفیں اللہ ہی کے لئے ہیں اور معتزلہ کہتے ہیں کہ الف لام حمد میں عہد کے لئے ہے کیونکہ یہ حضرات افعال عبد کی تخلیق کو ہندہ ہی کی طرف منسوب کرتے ہیں میں پس تقدیری عبارت ہوگی "المحامد التي تتعلق بالاعيان دون الاعراض لله تعالى" اعتراض: لام کو استغراق جنس کے لئے ماننے کی صورت میں ایک اشکال ہے اور یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں جملہ تعریفات خواہ اعیان سے متعلق ہوں یا اعراض سے اللہ ہی کے ساتھ خاص ہونگی تو پھر یوں کہنا " حمدت فلاما علی شجاعتہ" کہ میں نے فلاں کی اس کی بہادری پر تعریف کی کہنا صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
جواب: اس کا یہ ہے کہ یہ بھی حقیقت میں تعریف اللہ ہی کی طرف لوٹے گی کیونکہ مخلوق کی تعریف کسی صفت پر یا فعل پر در حقیقت خالق کی ہی حمد ہے۔
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Translation: I begin with the name of Allah, who is immensely merciful and infinitely compassionate. Commentary: Allama Ibn Qayyim al-Misri (may mercy be upon him) began his book Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair following the Quran and the Prophet's hadith 'Every matter that does not begin with the mention of Allah and Bismillah is cut off' by starting with basmalah and hamd. Objection: The hadith of basmalah and the hadith of hamd apparently conflict; acting on one causes the other to be missed. Answer: It is possible to combine them by carrying the hadith of basmalah on real beginning and the hadith of hamd on additional beginning, or basmalah on real beginning and hamd on customary beginning. The reason for carrying basmalah on real beginning is that 'Allah' indicates the essence and 'hamd' indicates an attribute, and essence precedes attributes. The 'ba' in 'bismillah' is for seeking help or for blessing. 'Allah' is a proper noun for the exalted essence; the chosen view is that it is non-derived, as held by Khalil al-Nahwi, Imam Sayyid, many usulis and jurists. 'Allah' is the name of that necessarily existent essence which possesses all perfect attributes and is free from deficiency and signs of deficiency. The word 'Allah' is the leader of all names. Applying it to anyone else is forbidden; Allah has exclusively reserved this name for His holy essence, and no one has been able to name themselves Allah. Some polytheists tried to name their idols Allah, but Allah turned their minds to 'al-Lat' instead. 'Al-Rahman al-Rahim': 'Rahman' is on the pattern of 'fa'lan' derived from 'rahma' like 'ghadban' from 'ghadab', and 'Rahim' is on the pattern of 'fa'il' also from 'rahma'. 'Rahman' has greater intensification than 'Rahim'; therefore scholars say 'Rahman of this world and the hereafter, and Rahim of this world'. Also, increase in letters indicates increase in meaning; 'Rahman' has more letters, thus it is more intensive. Attributing mercy to Allah means bestowing good. 'Rahim' is mentioned after 'Rahman' as a complement, both are in the genitive because they are attributes of Allah, and they are attributes of praise whose purpose is... Scholars of grammar differ on whether 'Rahman' is declinable or not; some require the pattern 'fa'lan' for non-declinability, so 'Rahman' is non-declinable; others consider properness as sufficient, so it is declinable. 'All praise is due to Allah for what He has bestowed, and may Allah send blessings and peace upon our master Muhammad.' Translation: All praises are exclusively for Allah for His blessings, and may Allah's mercy and peace descend upon our master Muhammad. Commentary: The definite article 'al-' is used for: (1) external specific, (2) mental specific, (3) comprehensive (istighraq), or (4) generic definition. The original among these is 'ahd' (specific), then 'istighraq', then 'jins' (generic), because when 'al-' enters a word that indicates a quiddity without it, it is better to carry it on a new benefit rather than on natural definition. The new benefit here is either specific definition or comprehensive generic definition, and specific definition is better than comprehensive, because some individuals of the genus are mentioned as external specific or mental specific, and carrying the 'al-' on external specific or mental specific is better than carrying it on all individuals, because the specific is certain and the general is probable. Then scholars differed: when 'al-' enters a singular or plural, the majority of usulis and grammarians hold that in both cases it gives comprehensive benefit, provided it is praiseworthy. Abu Ali al-Farsi says that in both cases it is for absolute genus, not comprehensive. This is also one of two opinions of Abu Hashim al-Mu'tazili; his second opinion is that for singular it is absolute genus and for plural it is absolute plural, not comprehensive, unless there is another proof. Now that you know the detail, know that the 'al-' in 'al-hamd' is for genus, meaning praise is exclusively for Allah. Another opinion says it is for comprehensive genus, i.e., all praises are for Allah. The Mu'tazila say it is for specific, because they attribute the creation of actions to the servant themselves. So the implied expression would be 'Al-hamd li Allah' meaning 'Praiseworthy acts related to substances, not accidents, are for Allah'. Objection: If we accept 'al-' as comprehensive genus, an objection arises: then all praises, whether related to substances or accidents, would be exclusively for Allah, so saying 'I praised so-and-so for his bravery' would not be correct. Answer: This too in reality returns to praising Allah, because praising a creation for a quality or action is in reality praise of the Creator.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to his commentary on Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair. He begins by explaining why he starts with the basmalah and hamd, following the Quranic and Prophetic practice. He then addresses an apparent contradiction between the hadith emphasizing basmalah and the hadith emphasizing hamd, resolving it by distinguishing between real and attributive beginnings. The bulk of the passage is a detailed linguistic and theological analysis of the key words: 'Allah' (its non-derived nature and exclusivity), 'al-Rahman' and 'al-Rahim' (their derivation and intensification), and the definite article 'al-' in 'al-hamdu'. For 'al-', the author explores its four uses (specific, mental, comprehensive, generic) and argues that it is best understood as generic or comprehensive in this context, with a discussion of scholarly differences including the Mu'tazila position. He concludes by rebutting an objection that using 'al-' comprehensively would make praising others invalid, explaining that all praise ultimately returns to Allah. This introduction sets the methodological groundwork for the usul al-iftaa discussions to follow.

Key Terms
بسم الله (Bismillah): The phrase 'In the name of Allah' used by the author to begin his book, following prophetic tradition.
الحمد لله (Al-hamdu lillah): All praise is due to Allah; the author explains the definite article 'al-' as indicating genus or comprehensive praise.
الرحمن الرحيم (Al-Rahman al-Rahim): Two names of Allah derived from 'rahma'; 'Rahman' is more intensive and applies to both worlds, 'Rahim' primarily to this world.
اللّٰه (Allah): The proper noun for the necessary existent with all perfect attributes; non-derived and exclusive to Allah.
لام العهد (Lam al-'ahd): The definite article used for a specific (known) referent, either external or mental.
لام الاستغراق (Lam al-istighraq): The definite article used to indicate comprehensive inclusion of all individuals of a genus.

According to the passage, what is the main difference between 'Rahman' and 'Rahim'?
A) 'Rahman' is derived from 'rahma' while 'Rahim' is not.
B) 'Rahman' has greater intensification and applies to both worlds, while 'Rahim' applies mainly to this world.

Key Takeaway
Linguistic precision and the reconciliation of apparent contradictions are foundational to Hanafi usul al-iftaa.

Introduction and Front Matter
advanced
8 min
Functions of the Definite Article (Alif Lam) in Hanafi Legal Interpretation
Linguistic analysis of the opening phrase 'Alhamdulillah' focusing on the definite article

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four functions of the definite article (alif lam) and apply the Hanafi preference for 'ahd' over 'istighraq' when interpreting legal texts.

Core Idea
The definite article primarily indicates customary reference, not universal coverage, shaping how general commands are applied.

The opening phrase of every classical Hanafi work, 'Alhamdulillah', is more than a pious invocation. It embodies a subtle linguistic argument about how the definite article functions in Arabic. This lesson unpacks that argument, revealing how a seemingly simple 'al' can determine whether a legal ruling applies to all instances or only to a customary subset. Understanding this is foundational for any mufti who interprets Quranic or Hadith texts.

Guided Path
1
List the four functions of 'al'
From the passage, extract the four uses of the definite article: external reference (ahd khariji), mental reference (ahd dhihni), comprehensive coverage (istighraq), and definition of the genus (ta'rif al-jins). Write them in Arabic and English.
The passage also discusses a hierarchy; note the author's preferred order.
2
Understand the author's hierarchy
The author states that the primary function is 'ahd' because it provides a new benefit (fa'idah jadidah) by specifying some individuals, which is more certain than including all. Explain why specifying is more certain.
Refer to the reasoning: 'some is certain, all is probable'.
3
Identify the disagreement among scholars
The passage mentions different views: majority of usul scholars and Arabists hold that 'al' on a common noun indicates istighraq; Abu 'Ali al-Farisi and some Mu'tazila argue for absolute genus. Note these positions and which one the author seems to favor.
The author indicates that in 'al-hamd', 'al' is for the genus, but his general hierarchy prioritizes 'ahd'.
4
Apply the analysis to a legal text
Consider the Quranic phrase 'al-sariq' (the thief) in the verse on amputation. Using the author's preference for 'ahd', determine whether 'al-sariq' means 'the specific thief known in custom' or 'every thief universally'. Explain the legal consequence.
This step connects linguistic theory to fiqh application.
5
Trace the implications for iftaa
A Hanafi mufti uses this hierarchy when interpreting general commands. If 'al' indicates 'ahd', the ruling applies only to the customary case, not to all possible instances. Provide an example from a contemporary fatwa scenario.
E.g., 'al-bay' (the sale) in a hadith may refer to the customary sale, excluding unusual contracts.

رحمن کے انصراف اور عدم انصراف میں علماء نحاۃ کا اختلاف ہے۔ بعض نے منع غیر منصرف کے لئے انتظار فعانہ [؟] کو شرط قرار دیا ہے، ان کے نزدیک رحمن منع غیر منصرف ہے۔ اور جنہوں نے وجود تعلی [؟] کو ضروری قرار سے زیادہ سے زیادہ لازم آتا ہے کہ وہ ازل میں بندوں کی حمد کے ساتھ متصف نہیں تھا لیکن جن کمالات کی وجہ سے وہ حمد کے ساتھ متصف ہے وہ کمالات اس کے اندر ازل سے ہی ہیں۔ صاحب کتاب علیہ الرحمہ نے یہاں جملہ فعلیہ کے مقابلہ میں جملہ اسمیہ اختیار کیا ہے وہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ جملہ اسمیہ دوام اور ثبات پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور جملہ فعلیہ تجدد اور حدوث پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ على ما انعم میں ما مصدر یہ ہے موصول اسی نہیں ہے ماضی ہے اور مصدر قیاسی تصادیہ ہے اگر چہ اس کا استعمال اہل لغت کے نزدیک زیادہ تر متروک ہے اور صلاۃ کا استعمال زیادہ ہوتا ہے۔ صلاة : میں الف واؤ سے بدل کر آیا ہے اور الف کے ساتھ ہی لکھا جاتا ہے لیکن پھر دعاء کے معنی میں استعمال ہونے لگا لہذا یہ دعا کے معنی میں مجاز ہے۔ علامہ سعدالدین تفتازانی فرماتے ہیں کہ دعا میں حقیقیہ لغویہ ہے اور ارکان مخصوصہ میں مجاز ہے ارکان مخصوصہ کے دعا پر مشتمل ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ جمہور علما بھی اس کے قائل ہیں۔ صلاۃ کی نسبت اگر اللہ کی طرف ہو تو رحمت اور فرشتوں کی طرف نسبت ہو تو استغفار اور بندوں کی طرف ہو تو دعا اور جانوروں اور نباتات کی طرف نسبت ہو تو تسبیح وغیرہ کے معنی میں مستعمل ہوتا ہے۔
There is disagreement among grammarians regarding the declension of 'Rahman' and its non-declension. Some have made 'intizar al-fi'lah [؟] a condition for non-declension; according to them, 'Rahman' is non-declinable. And those who considered 'wujud al-ta'li [؟] necessary, according to them it is declinable. 'Al-hamdu lillahi 'ala ma an'am wa salla Allahu 'ala sayyidina Muhammadin wa sallam.' Translation: All praises are specific to Allah for His bestowal of blessings, and may Allah's mercy and peace descend upon our master Muhammad, peace be upon him. Explanation: The definite article 'al' is used for (1) external reference [؟], (2) mental reference [؟], (3) comprehensive coverage, or (4) definition of the genus. But the primary among these is 'ahd' (reference), then istighraq, then definition of the genus, because when the word on which the 'al' enters indicates the essence without the 'al', then it is more appropriate to consider the 'al' as conveying a new benefit rather than defining the nature. The new benefit here is either in the definition of 'ahd' or comprehensive coverage of the genus, and definition by 'ahd' is more appropriate than comprehensive coverage because some individuals of the genus are mentioned on the basis of external reference and mental reference, and it is more appropriate to place the word on some external reference or mental reference than on all individuals, because some is certain and all is probable. Then scholars differed: when the 'al' enters a singular or plural noun, the majority of usul scholars and Arabists hold that in both cases the 'al' gives the benefit of comprehensive coverage, provided that the noun is a common noun. Abu 'Ali al-Farisi says that in both cases it is for the absolute genus, not for comprehensive coverage; this is one of two opinions of Abu Bashm [؟] al-Mu'tazili. His other opinion is that in the singular it is for the absolute genus, and in the plural it is for the absolute plural, not for comprehensive coverage, but based on some other evidence. Now that you know the details, know that the 'al' in 'al-hamd' is for the genus, meaning the context specifically relates praise to Allah. The second opinion is that the 'al' is for comprehensive coverage of the genus, meaning that all praises are only for Allah. The Mu'tazila say that the 'al' in 'al-hamd' is for 'ahd' because they attribute the creation of acts of servants to Allah alone. So the implied expression would be: 'The praises that relate to entities, not accidents, are for Allah.' Objection: If the 'al' is considered for comprehensive coverage of the genus, a problem arises: in that case, all praises, whether related to entities or accidents, would be specific to Allah, so saying 'I praised so-and-so for his courage' would not be correct. Answer: This also in reality returns to praising Allah, because praise of a creature for a quality or action is in reality praise of the Creator. 'Hamd' is praise of a volitional act with the tongue, whether in return for a favor or not. It is said: 'I praised him for his general beneficence and for his courage.' 'Shukr' is praise in return for a favor, whether with the tongue or with the limbs, as a poet said: 'Your bestowal of blessings upon me results in three things: my hand, my tongue, and my hidden heart.' Between 'hamd' and 'shukr' there is a relationship of general and specific from one aspect. 'Madh' is defined as praise of a non-volitional act with the tongue. It is said: 'I praised Allah and thanked Him.' 'Al-hamdu lillah' is, in terms of construction, a declarative sentence, but in meaning it is performative. And there is a doubt regarding the performative meaning: because performative is said to be 'the affirmation of something that was not previously established,' which would imply that before the praise of servants, Allah's noble essence was not praised (mahmud). The answer is that this only implies that He was not described with the praise of servants in eternity, but the perfections due to which He is described with praise are present in Him from eternity. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, chose a nominal sentence over a verbal sentence because a nominal sentence indicates continuity and permanence, while a verbal sentence indicates renewal and occurrence. In 'ala ma an'am', 'ma' is a masdariyya infinitive, not a relative pronoun; this is the preferred view. Some say that 'ma' is ta'limiyya (instructive) or for 'musahat' (companionship) in the meaning of 'ni' or 'ma'a'. It is also possible to consider 'ma' as for height (isti'la'), and the reference with it is to the value of praise. 'Salla' is a past tense verb, and its analogical infinitive is 'tasliyah', although its usage among lexicographers is mostly abandoned, and 'salah' is used more frequently. 'Salah': the alif is a substitute for waw, and it is written with alif, but in the Qur'an it is used with waw. The meaning of 'salah' is literally 'movement of the hips' (tahrik al-salawain), and in prayer the meaning of moving the hips is found, so the specific actions were named 'salah'. Then it began to be used in the meaning of supplication (du'a), because just as prayer involves humility and submission, so does supplication. Imam Zamakhshari in al-Kashshaf mentioned that 'salah' is the name for specific actions, then it was used by way of mercy in the meaning of compassion, then it came to be used in the meaning of supplication, so it is a metaphorical usage for supplication. Allamah Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani says that the literal linguistic meaning is supplication, and it is metaphorical for the specific actions because the specific actions contain supplication. The majority of scholars hold this view. When 'salah' is attributed to Allah, it means mercy; to angels, it means seeking forgiveness; to believers, it means supplication; to animals and plants, it means glorification etc.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is the introductory commentary of the book, explaining the opening phrase 'Al-hamdu lillah' from linguistic, theological, and legal-philosophical perspectives. The author begins with a peripheral note on the declension of the word 'Rahman' (whether it is diptote or triptote) among grammarians, then moves to the central analysis of the definite article 'al' in 'al-hamd'. He lists four possible functions of 'al': external reference (ahd khariji), mental reference (ahd dhihni), comprehensive coverage (istighraq), and definition of the genus (ta'rif al-jins). He states that the primary function is 'ahd' (customary reference), due to the principle that the definite article should be understood to add a new benefit; and specifying some individuals is more certain than including all. He then discusses scholarly disagreements: the majority of usul scholars and Arabists hold that 'al' on a common noun indicates istighraq, while Abu 'Ali al-Farisi and some Mu'tazila argue for absolute genus. In the specific context of 'al-hamd', the author indicates that the 'al' is for the genus (jins), meaning praise is exclusive to Allah, but the Mu'tazila interpret it as 'ahd' because they believe all acts are created by Allah. An objection regarding praising creatures for their attributes is answered by stating that such praise ultimately reverts to the Creator. The passage then defines 'hamd' as volitional praise with the tongue, 'shukr' as praise in return for a favor (by tongue or limbs), and 'madh' as praise of non-volitional acts. The relationship between 'hamd' and 'shukr' is general and specific from one aspect. The author clarifies that 'al-hamdu lillah' is a nominal sentence indicating permanence, chosen over a verbal sentence to imply continuity. He addresses a doubt: if the phrase is performative (insha'), it might imply that Allah was not praised before; the answer is that the perfections for which He is praised are eternal, not the actual praise of servants. Finally, he provides a detailed linguistic analysis of the word 'salah' (prayer): its etymology, literal meaning (movement of the hips), and its transferred usages in religious terminology (supplication, mercy, forgiveness, etc.), citing authorities like Zamakhshari and Taftazani. This entire section serves as a foundational front matter, establishing the linguistic and theological principles that underpin the legal maxims discussed later in the book.

Key Terms
ال (الف لام) (al (alif lam)): The definite article in Arabic, which can indicate external reference (عهد خارجی), mental reference (عهد ذهنی), comprehensive coverage (استغراق), or definition of the genus (تعریف جنس). The author prioritizes 'ahd' as the primary function.
حمد (hamd): Praising someone with the tongue for a volitional act, whether or not it is in return for a favor. Distinct from 'shukr' (gratitude for a favor) and 'madh' (praise for a non-volitional act).
شکر (shukr): Praising someone in return for a favor, which can be done with the tongue, heart, or limbs.
صلاة (salah): Linguistically means supplication (du'a) or movement of the hips; technically refers to the specific ritual prayer. When attributed to Allah means mercy, to angels istighfar, to humans supplication, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary function of the definite article (ال) in the phrase 'الحمد لله'?
A) Comprehensive coverage (استغراق) of all praises
B) Customary reference (عهد) to particular praises
C) Definition of the genus (تعریف جنس)
D) Indication of exclusivity (اختصاص)

Key Takeaway
The definite article's primary function is customary reference ('ahd'), and this determines how general commands are applied in Hanafi legal interpretation.
